A Glorious Page of Battle History at Xifengkou

Five Hundred Brave Soldiers of Our Army Heroically Sacrificed

Over Ten Thousand Enemy Soldiers Died Under the Blades of Broadswords

A dispatch from Beiping states that the battle at Xifengkou has been extremely fierce, and our side has achieved a great victory. Approximately ten thousand or more enemy soldiers from two brigades were surrounded and slashed to death by the troops of Song Zheyuan. This battle involved extremely brave sacrifices by our frontline soldiers and truly added a page of glory to our nation. The Beiping Liaoning-Jilin-Heilongjiang People's Support Association previously sent a representative to Xifengkou for comfort and support, Quan Shaowu, who returned to Beiping on the evening of the 13th. According to his detailed account of the events, we record the following:

Five Hundred Brave Soldiers Heroically Sacrificed - On the 9th of the month, the troops of Wan Fulin retreated from Kuancheng towards Xifengkou. The enemy army closely pursued from behind. Taking advantage of the fact that our new troops had not yet taken over the defense, they occupied the Xifengkou mountain. Further relying on their victory and showing contempt for the enemy, all four brigades of the 13th climbed the mountain, and all their military equipment and artillery were moved into the mountain as well. At this time, the troops of Song Zheyuan were still in Zunhua. Upon hearing of the change, they immediately issued orders on the morning of the 9th to advance towards Xifengkou. The journey was approximately 150 li. By 4 PM, they had reached the vicinity of the Great Wall. Upon seeing the Japanese army guarding the city, all the soldiers were filled with righteous indignation. The vanguard unit, the division of Feng Zhi'an, immediately selected elite soldiers from the battalion. At dusk, each holding a broadsword and stripped to the waist, they advanced. They climbed onto the city walls and immediately drew their swords to slash and kill. The Japanese soldiers guarding the city were caught completely unprepared. Many were killed before they could even retaliate. In a short time, all one thousand Japanese soldiers guarding the city were killed, and the five hundred soldiers of our side who bravely killed the enemy were also sacrificed at the same time. Only about twenty survivors remained. This heroic and tragic event truly won great glory for our nation and inspires the admiration of the people of our country.

Night Attack on Enemy Camp, Killing Thousands of Enemies - At the meeting at Fengkou, the strategy for attacking was discussed. At 12 AM that night, a night attack was launched on the enemy camp. Each army advanced stealthily. With extreme speed, they fiercely struck the enemy's second line of defense. That night, over a thousand enemies were killed. Our side also suffered casualties. At 9 AM on the 10th, the enemy ordered a general attack, bombarding our positions with heavy artillery. Their bombardment tactics were no different from those used in the European war. The density of the shells was similar to that of bullets. When the enemy heavily bombarded, our army retreated from the original line of defense, lying prone and still, waiting. After more than three hours, the enemy's bombardment gradually subsided, and our army rapidly advanced to the original line of defense. At this time, the sky was dim, and yellow sand covered the surface. Our army, lying prone, advanced to a point three or four meters away from the enemy and launched a fierce surprise attack. In this battle, another thousand enemies were killed, and morale was greatly boosted.

Fierce Battle All Night, Surrounding the Enemy - On the night of the 10th, our side launched another night attack, sending two columns of soldiers to bypass the mountain peaks from the left and right to carry out an encirclement. The fierce battle that night was the most intense. The enemy was caught off guard. By dawn on the 11th, the two regiments of our army advancing from the left and right had converged at Dongjiakou behind the enemy, completing the encirclement. A large encirclement, twenty li in circumference, was formed by our army. The enemy army was in internal disarray. Over ten cannons placed behind the army were seized by our army. By the night of the 11th, the enemy's artillery unit had been completely destroyed by our army. The enemy's morale was extremely demoralized. They scrambled to hide in the mountains. From the night of the 11th onwards, our army continuously dispatched broadsword teams to search the enemy in the mountains overnight. Two-thirds of the prisoners were Japanese soldiers. In addition to the puppet troops, there were also Koreans mixed among them. As of the 13th, only two mountains had not yet been completely searched. All the other mountains had been cleared. The number of captured spoils of war was very large. The detailed numbers will take one or two more days to ascertain.

The Key to Victory Lies in Swiftness - In the Battle of Xifengkou, ten thousand enemies were annihilated in three days and nights, and spoils of war worth approximately ten million yuan were captured. This was the first major victory since the outbreak of the Rehe Incident. There were three main reasons for being able to achieve victory: First, the army was swift in movement. The army was most skilled in running exercises and moved swiftly on the battlefield, often catching the enemy off guard and forcing its way into key positions, launching fierce attacks, and causing the enemy to suffer repeated heavy blows. Second, night battles were used. When fighting at night, the enemy's aircraft, tanks, and other modern weapons could not be used. This precisely made up for the shortcomings of our army's lack of equipment. Furthermore, the agile movements of our army further reduced the enemy's combat power. Third, the broadsword team charged. This was a special organization of our Northwest Army and was feared by the Japanese army, which relied solely on scientific weapons. When the broadsword team charged, the enemy often did not have time to resist within a few feet, and heads were immediately separated from bodies. However, this type of charge must be carried out when the enemy is not expecting it. This time, our army had these three advantages, coupled with the soldiers' brave spirit and determination to resist the enemy to the death, so they achieved a great victory in a very short period of time.

Map of the Battle Zone at the Key Points of the Great Wall 52

The People of the War Zone Unanimously Support - The people of the war zone deeply admire the soldiers who resolutely defend the country and resist foreign aggression. Without waiting to be supplied, the local villagers, regardless of the size of their households, steamed buns to supply the army. In terms of supplies, there will be no problem for ten days. However, relying solely on the supply of the villagers is ultimately inappropriate. The rear should think of more practical ways to adequately supply the soldiers at the front. According to Quan Shaowu, it has been decided to launch a memorial for the five hundred and seventy soldiers of Feng's division who bravely killed the enemy and sacrificed their lives, in order to commend them. Quan will carry a large amount of comfort items back to Xifengkou on the morning of the 15th to comfort the army and prepare to bring back a portion of the spoils of war as a souvenir when returning to Beiping. (March 15th)

Luo Wen'gan Denies Direct Negotiations 53

Jiang's Opinion Is the Government's Established Policy

Direct Sino-Japanese Negotiations Are Purely Groundless Rumors

A dispatch from Beiping states that Foreign Minister Luo Wen'gan went to Beiping on the 14th from Baoding to meet with Jiang [Jieshi], and met with He Yingqin, Huang Shaohong, and others. On the 15th, he left Beiping and returned to Nanjing. Before leaving, he issued the following remarks: (This time, I went to Baoding to visit Chairman Jiang. The matters discussed were all very satisfactory. Chairman Jiang's opinion on Japan is also the government's established policy. The rumors of direct Sino-Japanese negotiations are purely groundless. I don't know where such rumors originated. Since the September 18th Incident, our country has first appealed to the League of Nations on the basis of reason. I have also accepted the resolution of the League of Nations and cannot overturn the previous resolution. Since our country is cooperating with the League of Nations, we will proceed according to the League of Nations' report. In any case, we will not change our attitude. For example, a company has a contract with someone and cannot break it. I have solemnly declared this point to the foreign press. The visits of the British, American, and French envoys were only social conversations. As for the report that the government has formulated a new diplomatic policy, I am afraid it is just speculation. As for the so-called new diplomatic policy, I really don't know about it, and I haven't officially heard of it. My travels between Nanjing, Beiping, and Baoding are not for any major task. I am only gathering with the authorities to have discussions. This is a personal action. The problem with Japan cannot be solved solely through diplomatic means. Apart from fighting it, there is really no other good way. The fierce battle and great victory of Song Zheyuan's troops at Xifengkou is truly the glory of our Chinese nation.) (15th)

Yan Discusses the Results of Meeting with Jiang 54

Shanxi to Dispatch Three Armies to Take Charge of Defense of Chahar

The Chairman of Chahar Province Will Absolutely Not Be Changed

A dispatch from Taiyuan states that Yan Xishan went to Shijiazhuang on the 11th to meet with Jiang [Jieshi] to discuss major plans for resisting Japan. He returned to Taiyuan from Shijiazhuang on the evening of the 12th. According to Yan's remarks on the results of meeting with Jiang in Shijiazhuang, he said: (Both Chairman Jiang and I believe that the deterioration of national affairs is extremely distressing. In the future, we can only unite as a nation, unite sincerely, each fulfill their responsibilities, and carry out a planned and determined joint struggle to save the country from danger. It is rumored that the defense of Chahar will be taken over by the Shanxi army. Chahar is a crucial defense line for Rehe, with a length of over one thousand li. It is still far from enough to fulfill this defense solely by exerting the full strength of the Jin-Sui army. This time, the anti-Japanese war is under the unified command of the Beiping Military Branch. The Jin-Sui army has dispatched three armies under the command of the Beiping Military Branch. Where they will be dispatched and what tasks they will undertake will be determined by the orders of the Beiping Military Branch. It is not that the Jin-Sui army will exclusively take over the defense of Chahar. As for the military expenses of the Jin-Sui army, the regular expenses will still be borne by Jin-Sui, while the wartime expenses and logistics expenses will be borne by the Beiping Military Branch. Chairman Jiang will temporarily reside in North China to preside over everything. The news that Fu Zuoyi will preside over Chahar and Hebei is definitely not true. Such rumors are enough to disrupt the anti-Japanese front. Even if the central government has such an order, Fu will definitely firmly decline. It must not be allowed for rumors of power struggles to arise amidst the anti-Japanese reality. (14th)

Chen Jitang Arrives in Shantou 55

Calls Party, Military, and Political Circles for Instructions

Will Return to the Province Via Meixian and Huizhou

A dispatch from Shantou states that Chen Jitang departed from the province on the 2nd aboard the Hai Zhou warship for an eastern inspection. On the 3rd, he arrived at Shanwei in Haifeng County, and immediately disembarked there. On the 4th, he convened instructions for all sectors in the county seat of Haifeng. At noon, he went to Lufeng. On the 5th, he gave instructions in Lufeng. On the 6th, he went to Lihu in Puning to inspect Liusha with Division Commander Zhang Ruigui. It was heard that he also went to Guiyu and Xiashan in Chaoyang to discuss plans for the aftermath of the Nanshan bandit area. At 2 PM on the 7th, Chen arrived in Jieyang from Chaoyang. County Magistrate Li Henian sent out a guard cadre team to temporarily impose martial law for protection. After Chen had dinner in Jieyang, he set off for Shantou, arriving at 9:30 PM. Those who came with him included Division Commanders Huang Renhuan and Zhang Ruigui, as well as more than thirty staff members and guards. The Chief of Staff of the Eastern District Pacification Headquarters, Chen Zhongying, the Municipal Party Committee member Yu Zuming, and Mayor Zhai Zongxin all welcomed him at the pier. That night, Chen stayed at the Eastern District Pacification Headquarters, while Zhang and Huang stayed at the Sihai Hotel. Chen immediately summoned the county magistrates and local leaders of the Chaoshan area to Shantou for instructions, and reported on the implementation of the three-year plan in Guangdong Province, and consulted with all sectors.

At noon on the 8th, nine heavily wounded soldiers were carried on canvas stretchers to the Qizhong Municipal Hospital. Accompanying them were Red Cross personnel. It was said that on the night of the 6th, in Jieyang City, while escorting Chen Jitang through Chengbeimen Street, there was a sudden roaring sound followed by chaotic gunfire for about a few minutes. More than ten people were killed and injured on the spot, and the soldiers were also injured. Fortunately, Chen was unharmed. On the 8th, all sectors of Shantou held a welcoming meeting. Chen declined to attend the meeting, and instead hosted all sectors at the Eastern District Pacification Headquarters. The Municipal Party Committee issued a notice to each organization to send two people to the meeting. More than two hundred people attended that day, and the security was tight. Chen went downstairs to take his seat at 3:30 PM, and gave a speech to all sectors for an hour, regarding national difficulties, construction issues, national defense, reforms, and the abolition of heavy taxes and miscellaneous levies to relieve the suffering of the people. After the meeting, Chen told the press that Guangdong's support army for Rehe has been determined, but the choice of commander has not been decided. He also planned to send personnel to Guangxi to investigate the militia organization in order to organize the people into disciplined forces. On the 9th, Chen summoned the leaders of political parties for instructions. On the 10th, he summoned the officers of the Third Army and the staff of the Eastern District Pacification Headquarters for instructions. In the afternoon, he visited the Poor People's Handicraft Institute. After returning to the Pacification Headquarters, he summoned the leaders of the Chamber of Commerce to meet at the Eastern District Pacification Headquarters to inquire about the business conditions of Chaoshan. That evening at 8 PM, Chen left Shantou by special train for Chaozhou. Huang Renhuan, Chen Zhongying, and others accompanied him. It was heard that he would also go to Meixian and Xingning, and then return to the province via Huizhou. (March 11th)

Suzhou Provincial Party Committee Investigates the Party Committee's Accusation

Zhang Zongmin, the reorganization committee member of the Wu County Party, and Yao Hongzhi, the standing committee member of the Anti-Japanese Association, were accused by party members Gu Baiyu and others to the Provincial Party Department of stealing and selling enemy goods, harboring gambling and opium dens, receiving kickbacks, and employing cronies. The Provincial Party Department specially dispatched Wang Bonian to Suzhou for investigation. After Wang arrived in Suzhou, he is secretly investigating from all sides. It is heard that he has already found some clues and will return to the province today (18th) to report his findings.

Appeal to Exempt or Reduce Land Tax Approved by the Executive Yuan 56

Regarding the case of the continued imposition of land tax in Jiangsu Province, representatives such as Qian Ding from the four counties of Wuxian, Kunshan, Changshu, and Wujiang were previously elected to go to Nanjing to appeal. Now it is known that Qian and others have received an order from the Executive Yuan, stating that the claim of repeated water disasters, wars, and low rice prices leading to the economic collapse of the rural areas is still factual. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has been ordered to reduce or halve the additional land tax for the 21st year of the Republic in the counties that suffered water disasters and wars, according to the severity of the disaster.

Wuxi Jiangyin Murder Case Transferred to Wuxi for Trial

Sun Peiji, a resident of Xijie in Jiangyin City, who repairs rickshaws for a living, has a wife, Shi, and a concubine, Jiang (from Nanzha), living together in the same house. In the middle of July last year, a quarrel suddenly broke out between the wife and concubine, leading to discord in the family. On the night of October 2nd, Jiang suddenly committed suicide by jumping into the river. The county government of Jiangyin believed that Sun Peiji was suspected of murder, and arrested Sun for interrogation, detaining him until now without a verdict. Recently, Sun Peiji believed that the county had deliberately detained him and delayed the verdict, and appealed to the Suzhou Higher Court, requesting a transfer of jurisdiction. The acting County Magistrate Wang of the county government recently received an order from Chief Judge Lin, ordering Sun Peiji to be transferred to the Wuxi County Court for trial. After receiving the order, County Magistrate Wang prepared a document and sent police yesterday to escort Sun Peiji to Wuxi for delivery to the County Court for trial. In the afternoon, at around 5 PM, Prosecutor Shen opened the court for interrogation, and then ordered him to be detained pending further investigation and processing.

Dispute Over Donations for Aircraft Purchase 57

The cloth industry association of this county previously telegraphed the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Textile Industry Federation, proposing that the 80,000 to 90,000 yuan collected from the cotton yarn industry fund be used to support aircraft donations. The cloth industry businesses in Wujin and Cheng counties also unanimously agreed. Now it is learned that the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Textile Industry Federation has allocated the fund to open the Wanyuan Cotton Yarn Factory, with a planned capital of 300,000 yuan. The factory site is located in Suzhou, and industry representatives from various counties have been appointed as preparatory committee members to actively prepare. Therefore, a special letter was sent to the cloth industry association of this county for verification. After receiving the letter, the association plans to convene a meeting of industry members to solicit opinions. However, Cheng Jingdang, a local resident who was nominated as a preparatory committee member for the Wanyuan Cotton Yarn Factory, believes that during this time of national crisis, it is not the time to prepare for the factory, and donating to purchase aircraft is a matter of jointly facing the national crisis. Therefore, he declared that he was unwilling to attend the preparatory meeting of the factory and advocated to the counties that they should voluntarily withdraw the fund for donations if necessary. The Wujin Textile Industry Association also sent a letter to Cheng, expressing their unanimous opposition to the construction of the factory. In addition, the county government of this county received an order from the province, instructing it to immediately raise donations for the purchase of aircraft, organize a county aircraft donation collection and management committee, and stipulate that this county, as a first-class county, should raise 20,000 yuan in the first phase. After receiving the order, County Magistrate Chen has been actively carrying it out and has sent letters to the county chamber of commerce and the county party department, requesting them to quickly recommend one representative each to convene an establishment meeting to discuss implementation.

Changshu Water Police Seize a Large Batch of Farming Cattle

The water police stationed in Fushan Town in the eighth district received a tip-off the day before yesterday, stating that a large batch of farming cattle was being transported out of the country to be slaughtered in Shanghai. Secret slaughtering of farming cattle is prohibited by provincial regulations. Moreover, during this spring plowing season, attention should be paid. It was requested that the cattle be seized, and so on. After receiving the report, Captain Xie Pinfang immediately dispatched several policemen to wait at Dengshi. In the afternoon of the 15th, several boats were indeed found carrying dozens of farming cattle. The people, boats, and cattle were all detained and sent to the district office for processing.

Nantong The Ministry of Military Administration Auctions Off Military Land

The Ministry of Military Administration investigated and found that the land of the old Su Zhen and Langshan camps had been encroached upon by the Tonghai Reclamation Company. It was approved by the National Government that the company should pay compensation. If they were unwilling, the land would be recovered and auctioned off. The Ministry of Military Administration found that the company had not complied with the payment, so it specially consulted the Jiangsu Provincial Government, ordering the county magistrates of Nantong and Haimen to jointly auction it off and complete the process.

Relief After the Disaster in Lvsi 58

After Lvsi was looted by the mutinous soldiers of the provincial guerrilla team, in addition to borrowing 20,000 yuan from the county government and the chamber of commerce to relieve the market, the provincial government ordered the county on the 16th to prepare a detailed list of the damage for reporting to the province regarding the relief of the poor and the aftermath of the casualties.

Gaoyou Kidnapping Case in Nansongzhuang

At the home of farmer Zhang Yousheng in Nansongzhuang, the ninth district of the county, more than a dozen bandits suddenly came the night before, each holding firearms. They tied up his entire family with ropes, guarded by one bandit. The remaining bandits rushed into the bedroom and searched extensively, stealing clothing and silver dollars worth about 200 yuan. Not yet satisfied, the bandits kidnapped his son and demanded a ransom of 1,000 yuan, or they would tear up the ticket.

Jiaxing The Chief of the Water Police District Removed from Office and Transferred to the Province

Zhao Zezhou, the chief of the second water police district of Jiaxing, has been in office for several months. He has not achieved any success in arresting criminals, but he has been meticulous in sending people to search for opium dens and gambling dens and extort money on the pretext of doing so. Therefore, the rural areas have been greatly harassed, and local people have complained. Last month, Dafeng Temple Town was looted by bandits, and more than a dozen men and women were kidnapped. No bandit has been arrested yet. Recently, the province sent personnel to He [Jiaxing] for inspection and found out all kinds of things. The report to the province on the 16th led to the province's removal of Zhao from his post and his transfer to the province. Secretary Fang Xuchu was assigned to He as an agent.

Local News

Wang Jingwei Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon 59

Expresses Firm Refusal of Premiership

Cabinet Ministers of the National Government All Go to the Port to Welcome Him

Chairman Lin Sends Personal Letter Urging Wang to Return to Nanjing Immediately to Resume Duties

To Rest Briefly in Shanghai for Two or Three Days Before Proceeding to Nanjing

Wang Jingwei, the Premier of the Executive Yuan, took leave for medical treatment in Germany last December. Due to the pressing national crisis, he was repeatedly urged by telegram from the Central Government. He embarked on the French postal ship "Aramis" in Europe last month, arriving in Shanghai at 3:20 PM yesterday. Cabinet ministers of the National Government and representatives went to the port to welcome him. Song Ziwen, the Acting Premier of the Executive Yuan, took a customs launch to Songkou first, boarding the ship to greet him. After the ship docked, Wang, Song, and others transferred to a small launch to disembark at the New Customs Wharf, proceeding directly to the Chu residence on Avenue Albert for rest. Wang issued a written statement in the cabin, expressing his firm refusal of the premiership and recommending Song for the actual position. Wang himself wished to serve in the Central Party Headquarters. Song Ziwen also told reporters that Wang was weary from his journey and would rest briefly in Shanghai for two or three days before proceeding to Nanjing. Details are recorded as follows:

Enthusiastic Welcome Yesterday morning, those who went to the port to welcome Wang included Acting Premier Song Ziwen, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan Chu Minyi, Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua, and Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs Tang Haian, among others, who took the customs vessel "Kesheng" to the central pier of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company in Hongkou to welcome Wang. Others included Central Representative Ju Zheng, National Government Chairman's Representative Gao Lingbai, Military Affairs Commission Representative Zhu Peide, Legislative Yuan President Sun Ke's Representative Liu Weichi, Gansu Provincial Government Chairman Shao Lizi, Minister of Railways Gu Mengyu, Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo, Minister of the Navy Chen Shaokuan, Vice Minister of the Interior Gan Naiguang, Peng Xuepei, Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission Chen Shuren, Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Songhu Garrison Commander Dai Ji, Shanghai Public Security Bureau Chief Wen Hongen, Trademark Bureau Chief He Zhuoxian, Jiaotong University President Li Zhaohuan,

Central Committee members Bai Yun (left) and Song (right) photographed together on the ship (photographed by Li Zunyong)

Ti, Nanjing Mayor Shi Ying, Secretary-General of the Central Political Council Tang Youren, Mongolian Living Buddha Zhangjia's representative Meng He Batu'er, representatives of the Mongolian compatriots in Beijing and Military Affairs Commission Councillor De Ke Jike, Mongolian-Tibetan Affairs Commission Section Chief Wang Huimin, representatives of the Mongolian Cultural Advancement Association Li Yongxin and Liu Zhanyi, former Eurasian Aviation Corporation General Manager Wang Zhiyuan, Wing On Company General Manager Guo Shun, Chunghwa Daily Manager Lin Baisheng, Huang Renlin, Duan Xipeng, Wang's mother-in-law Madam Chen, Zeng Zhongming's wife, and over a hundred others. In addition, there were representatives from various organizations and groups, such as the dock workers' union, the woodworking union, and others, each holding welcome flags, causing the road to be congested by those wishing to see Wang's countenance. The Municipal Public Security Bureau also sent a military band to the pier to welcome him. French Consul-General Meyrier specially sent Police Commissioner Febvre and Deputy Commissioner Rabaute to represent him, and ordered Political Director Salley and Inspector Cheng Ziqing to lead many detectives to provide protection.

Security at the Wharf The security at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company wharf yesterday when Wang arrived was stricter than usual because there were over two thousand people there to welcome him. Therefore, police and detectives were stationed at the entrance of the outer Hongqiao, along the bank, at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company entrance and all points of embarkation and disembarkation, with strict precautions. On the wharf, the Public Security Team Inspector Xi Kui led over forty policemen, armed with loaded Mauser pistols, standing guard around the perimeter. On the Huangpu River, Water Patrol Team Captain Zhu Haishan led police in two small launches, patrolling the river. The Shanghai Municipal Council also sent over a dozen detectives to the Jianghai Customs Wharf to be on standby.

Arrival Circumstances The French ship Aramis, on which Wang and others were travelling, entered the Wusongkou at 1:15 PM yesterday and arrived at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's central pier in Hongkou at 2:30 PM. At 2:50 PM, it docked, and the military band began playing music to welcome them. Acting Premier Song Ziwen had already taken the customs vessel Kesheng with Secretary-General Chu Minyi, Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua, and Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs Tang Haian, among others, to board the Aramis in the river to meet Wang, offering their welcome with great enthusiasm. Wang then went with Song and others to the outer deck, removing his hat to nod and wave to those welcoming him. He then received the welcoming personnel who boarded the ship, shaking hands and exchanging greetings one by one. The scene was exceptionally warm. At 3:33 PM, Wang, accompanied by Song Ziwen, Chen Gongbo, Zhu Jiahua, and others, transferred to the customs vessel Kesheng, which sailed from the Jiangmian pier of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to the New Customs Wharf. Eleven members of the Customs Water Patrol Team and the Song residence guard escorted them on the ship. Chu Minyi, Tang Haian, and others took the Jinghui ship to the New Customs Wharf.

Wang's Demeanor Wang was wearing a gray Western suit yesterday, his face fuller than when he left the country, and his spirit was quite vibrant. Those accompanying Wang, besides his wife, Ms. Chen Bijun, and his daughter, Binbin, included Tie Ci, Zeng Zhongming, Secretary Li Haoju, attending physician Luo Guanglin, and German physician Noel, a total of seven people.

Gathering at the Chu Residence After disembarking, Wang was accompanied by Song Ziwen in his car, number 2844, first driving to Chu Minyi's residence at 408 Avenue Albert at 3:45 PM for rest. Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua and Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo visited Wang around 4 PM. Military Affairs Commission member Zhu Peide, Minister of the Navy Chen Shaokuan, Minister of Railways Gu Mengyu, Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission Chen Shuren, Gansu Provincial Chairman Shao Lizi, Central Committee member Zhang Qun, and Central Political Council Secretary Tang Youren also arrived one after another, gathering for thirty minutes. Then Song Ziwen left at 4:30 PM. The other ministers, except Chen Gongbo, Gu Mengyu, Zeng Zhongming, and Zhu Jiahua, who left after 6 PM, all left before 5 PM.

Urging Him to Resume Duties National Government Chairman Lin Zichao was unable to come to Shanghai personally to welcome Wang due to pressing political affairs. In addition to sending Chu Minyi as his representative, he also entrusted a personal letter to Chu Minyi to hand over to Wang, asking Wang to return to Nanjing upon arrival in Shanghai to preside over the central government and tide over the difficulties. Acting Premier Song Ziwen and Central Committee member Zhang Qun, representing Chairman Chiang, also earnestly urged Wang to return to Nanjing immediately to resume his duties. Wang expressed that he would definitely go to Nanjing within three days, but requested that Song be appointed as the actual Premier of the Executive Yuan, and that he himself would dedicate himself to the duties of the Central Party Headquarters, intending to return to Shanghai for recuperation after going to Nanjing.

Wang's Condition When Wang discussed his condition with those who met him yesterday, he claimed that his diabetes had been completely cured, but his liver disease, after developing cirrhosis, could no longer be reversed. He could only maintain its state and prevent further changes. He would leave the cirrhotic part to nature.

Proceeding to Nanjing in the Next Few Days After leaving the Chu residence, Acting Premier Song spoke with reporters in an off-the-record conversation. (Question) Premier Wang said during his arrival speech that he was resigning from the position of Premier of the Executive Yuan and reiterating his previous request. Will Acting Premier Song continue to act? (Answer) I do not yet know. (Question) You must have discussed it on the ship. (Answer) We only talked about what happened after we parted, not about this matter. (Question) When will Premier Wang go to Nanjing? (Answer) He is tired from his journey and may rest for a short time before proceeding to Nanjing in two or three days.

Written Statement Wang issued a statement in the cabin after arriving, saying, "I have suffered from liver disease for several years. When it flares up, I am unable to do anything. Last December, I entered the hospital established by Dr. Noel and discovered the source of the disease. After the doctor released his diagnosis last October, the central government, understanding the severity of my illness, granted me several months of leave to seek treatment in Europe. Dr. Noel had originally planned to return to Europe this spring but advanced his trip by several months to accompany me, taking care of me along the way. After arriving in Europe, I was introduced by Dr. Noel to the Tropical Diseases Specialist Hospital in Southern Germany and then to the Kaspar Spa Sanatorium in Czechoslovakia. My condition gradually improved. I had originally planned to finish treatment at the end of April and return to the country in early May. However, after hearing the news of the tragedy at Shanhaiguan, I set off in mid-February, hoping to face the national crisis with my colleagues and comrades. However, as my health has not yet fully recovered, I can only offer my humble contributions at the Central Party Headquarters. As for the position of Premier of the Executive Yuan, it is a busy and important responsibility. If I were to take it on reluctantly, I would only spoil things and harm the country. The current Premier of the Executive Yuan is already a capable and responsible person, but the title of 'Acting' has not been removed. I am determined to reiterate my previous request, hoping that the central government will approve it. Wang Jingwei, 17th."

Stops Acting as Premier

Premier Wang Recovers and Returns Home

The Central Government Already Has a Leader

From Yesterday Onwards, Ceases Acting

Telegram to the Central Government To the Central Political Conference of the National Government, Nanjing: Since September of last year, Premier Wang took leave due to illness to seek treatment elsewhere. Ziwen was ordered to act as Premier as Vice Premier, respectfully following the established rules, and勉將事. Every time Ziwen thought that Premier Wang was a pioneer of our party and a leader of the masses and at this time when the country is broken and a great crisis is upon us, the Central Committee is in urgent need of a leader, the hearts of the people should be bound together and unite to plan for revenge. It would not be enough to save this crisis and help this great difficulty unless Premier Wang presided over the overall plan. Heaven favored our nation, Premier Wang's old illness was cured, and he returned home. It could not be expressed in words. Ziwen will cease acting as Premier on the 17th of this month to follow Premier Wang in fulfilling his responsibilities, reporting respectfully, and begging for your consideration. Song Ziwen bows, 篠.

Ziwen will cease acting as Premier on the 17th of this month to follow Premier Wang in fulfilling his responsibilities, reporting respectfully, and begging for your consideration, etc. Ziwen held the post for several months, walking on thin ice, and was always mindful of the warning against disaster. Now that our leader, Premier Wang, has recovered and returned home, he can receive orders and teachings to work together in harmony. The bond is unbreakable, and the joy is inexpressible. This information is submitted respectfully, hoping for your consideration. Song Ziwen bows, 篠

Simpson to Return to England 63

Chairman Song Hosts Farewell Banquet

Presents Silver Cup to Commemorate Achievements

The Continental Daily News reports that Sir John Hope Simpson, Chairman of the National Flood Relief Commission, has completed his relief work and is scheduled to return to England on the 26th of this month. Chairman Song Ziwen hosted a banquet at the International Recreation Club last night to bid farewell to Simpson, presenting him with a silver cup to commemorate his service over the past eighteen months. Chinese dishes were served throughout the night. After several rounds of drinks, Song rose to present the cup, briefly stating that the Chinese people will forever be grateful for Sir John Hope Simpson's achievements. Had the National Government not abolished the order system, he would have requested the government to award him the highest order. Since this system has been abolished, he is presenting the silver cup before Sir John Hope Simpson returns to his country to mark his respect and admiration. He hopes that Sir John Hope Simpson will pass it down to his children and grandchildren as a lasting memory of his service to China. Simpson received the cup and thanked him, recounting the arduous work of the commission. Between November 1931 and June of the following year, the commission provided disaster relief to ten million famine victims, distributing food and assigning work to complete the levees. Such outstanding results, even compared to the disaster relief in India in 1895, are inferior. He then discussed the economic, social, and charitable importance of this initiative. Acting Premier Song estimated the cost and time for repairing levees and managing relief funds, which later turned out as expected. His predictions were accurate. However, this initiative is also politically important. In the past, people in the Jianghuai River basin viewed officials only as tax collectors for the government. In the future, they should know that the government pays attention to the welfare of the people. With Acting Premier Song's flood prevention plan, the people of the two major river basins can rest easy.

The members of this association are not sensitive and dare not remain silent. We believe that the plan for today is to take advantage of the fact that the people's hearts are invigorated, morale is high, and the whole country is mobilized for a long-term large-scale war of resistance, which is not enough to plan for recovery and save the country. It is even more necessary to abandon everything and devote the strength of the whole country to two things: First, we must actively counterattack Rehe. Facts have shown that the enemy's military deployment in Rehe Province has not yet been perfected. If we are internally united and persistent from beginning to end, we will break the cauldron, sink the boat, and fight to the death. Any sacrifice will be spared. If we win, we will return to our mountains and rivers. If we do not win, we will still make the enemy fall into misfortune. We are sure to know that there are no less than 200,000 volunteer comrades scattered throughout the East Province, and their latent power is still very great. If we truly provide continuous support and continue to motivate them to increase their active strength and promote their anti-Japanese spirit, they will surely rise up in response, take up their spears, and share the same hatred. In order to recover the Northeast, this is the direct work, and it is enough to contain the enemy's army in the counteroffensive against Rehe. This is the most important opportunity for anti-Japanese military affairs. In short, we should only carry out a positive counteroffensive against Rehe. No negotiations will be held until the lost territory is restored, and the enemy's conspiracy will be countered. In the Northeast, we should not only rely on the League of Nations' moral assistance, but also encourage our own actual power to seek self-salvation. For this reason, we urgently express our sincere desire. Northeast Association bows, 篠

Ministry of Finance Instructs Shanghai Chamber of Commerce

Announcing Abolition of Taels in Advance 65

All Accounts and Deeds to Be Changed to Silver Standard

The Ministry of Finance yesterday instructed the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, saying, "In order to comply with the order, the Ministry previously issued a notice that from the 10th of this month, all receipts and payments of public and private funds and all transactions shall be changed to silver coins, the silver exchange shall be abolished, and the exchange interest shall be used. It has been implemented for several days, and the situation on the market is quite convenient. The Ministry has now decided that the abolition of taels must be implemented in the shortest possible time. The Association is urgently ordered to immediately inform all colleagues that, from the date of receipt of the order, all accounts, deeds, and new loans should be uniformly changed to the silver coin standard and no longer used silver taels. It is hereby announced in advance, and all should follow and report."

Sun Dianying's Representative 67

Reports on the Bitter Fighting of Sun's Army

Hosts Press Conference Yesterday

Hopes for Nationwide Assistance

Zhang Youqun, the representative of Sun Dianying, the commander of the 41st Army, arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday to report to all sectors on the bitter fighting of the army in northern Rehe and to ask for assistance from the people of Shanghai. Zhang hosted a press conference at 7 p.m. yesterday at Yizhi Xiang on Fourth Horse Road, attended by more than 20 reporters from various newspapers. During the conference, Zhang gave a brief report, saying, "Our army set out from southern Jin to aid Rehe, traveling more than 3,000 li. On the 28th of the previous month, we reached the vicinity of Weichang and Chifeng. At that time, the enemy was approaching Chifeng. Fighting with the enemy began on the 1st of this month. On the evening of the 2nd, we lifted the siege of Chifeng. On the 3rd, we counterattacked the enemy and recovered Jianchangying, Cheshuipo, and other places. Unfortunately, Chengde fell, and our army's retreat was cut off. The enemy took advantage of the situation to surround us. Commander Sun personally led 30,000 soldiers in a bloody battle for two days and nights before breaking through the encirclement and concentrating the troops in the area. Since the continuous fighting, the enemy has not succeeded, but it is a desperate and isolated army, lacking supplies and ammunition. In forty degrees below zero, the soldiers are fighting in single clothes and with meager food. If they do not die under the enemy's artillery fire, they will inevitably freeze and starve to death, or die from injuries and illnesses without medical treatment. In addition to those killed in action at the front, dozens or hundreds of people die every day from freezing, starvation, and illness. The number of deaths at the rear is even greater than at the front. All kinds of tragic scenes are unbearable to witness. The entire army is still fighting the enemy in the area. We have sent the artillery brigade left behind in Jin to the front. As soon as the entire anti-Japanese military deployment is in place, we will counterattack Chengde. The soldiers at the front, though in the icy and snowy land, with inadequate clothing and food, are in high spirits. As long as there is food to fill our stomachs and ammunition is not lacking, we will fight the enemy to the end. We hope that the people of the whole country will rise up and support us so that we can resist for a long time."

Japanese Newspaper 74

Promoting the Popularity of Japanese Goods

Do Chinese Merchants Still Have Brains?

The Osaka Mainichi Shimbun reported on the 13th that the Chinese government's resistance in Rehe would only last three months. As a result, the Chinese government would inevitably change its diplomatic relations with Japan, and the economic circles in China could escape the harsh environment. Therefore, the trade of Japanese goods has gradually become active. For example, 1. Textiles: Although affected by the Rehe issue, they are not as affected by anti-Japanese sentiment as before, and sales are rebounding. 2. Cotton cloth: In January, 2,755 boxes were imported to Shanghai from Japan, and in February, 3,055 boxes were imported. Although the Rehe incident occurred, the import in February was more than in January. 3. Cotton yarn: Most are sold in small quantities, and more active trade can be expected in the future. 4. Sundries: More active than other commodities, and purchasing power is gradually recovering. 5. Sugar: Orders have been strong in recent days. The import of refined sugar to Shanghai last year reached 48,080 dan, and further progress is now expected. 6. Western paper: Since the anti-Japanese movement, it has been suppressed by Canadian and German products. Now that the anti-Japanese sentiment has weakened, there are also considerable imports and exports. 7. General industry: Recently, factories have expanded to three-tenths of their capacity. 8. Ships: Goods transshipped in Shanghai and sold to Hankou in mid-February amounted to about 3,000 tons, an increase of 500 tons compared to January. 9. Coal and industrial chemicals: Both have gradually recovered from pessimism.

Yesterday, the Japanese Shanghai Daily reported that the Osaka Textile Federation's survey of cotton cloth exports to China in mid-February showed a sharp increase to 13 million square yards, which is 35,288 square yards.

Wang Yansong Broadcasted a Children's Speech Yesterday 84

Titled "National Mobilization Should Start from One's Own Position"

Mr. Wang Yansong, Supervisory Committee Member of the City Party Headquarters and Standing Committee Member of the City Chamber of Commerce, was invited by the Zhongxi Pharmacy to broadcast last night. The recorded speech is as follows: Fellow compatriots, today I am here at the invitation of the Zhongxi Pharmacy radio station. My heart is filled with endless sadness and sorrow. Looking out over the Northeast, the mountains and rivers have changed color, and hundreds of millions of compatriots have become aliens. The local people are displaced, unable to live or die. Isn't this the sad state since the September 18th Incident two years ago? The Songhu bloody battle was subjected to trampling. The Zhabei Jiangwan Wusong and other districts became a white land. Isn't this the scar of January 28th? However, the Japanese invaders' ambitions have never diminished. They are still working day and night on their aggressive plans, dreaming of dominating the five continents. Their aggression will not end for a day, and our national crisis will not end for a day. Now Rehe has been lost, and the Gubei Xifeng sentry posts are in fierce battles. It is known that Pingjin Chahar and other places are definitely under pressure. The environment is dangerous and crises are lurking. Everyone knows this. At this time, I am afraid that some people will hold a very pessimistic attitude and say that China is hopeless. At the same time, there must be some people holding a kind of thinking, that is, they can't wait to kill to the northeast and fight the enemy to the death. In fact, a passive attitude and depressed mood cannot save the crisis, but it is also impossible to have the national people go to the front line to pick up the lance to kill the enemy. So, what should we citizens do at this time of national life and death? Our only way out is to advocate ("National Salvation from One's Own Position.") So I specifically chose this topic today ("National Mobilization Should Start from One's Own Position") to talk to everyone. The so-called national mobilization does not mean that every citizen takes a gun and dedicates his life to the frontier, bravely killing the enemy. Its meaning is that every national can start national work and anti-Japanese work from their own position, just to seek its effect, which can be as large as the effect of combat. Can merchants not kill the enemy to save the country? Who says they can't? The merchants' weapon against the enemy is economic severance, which is the anti-goods movement. The merchant's policy for saving the country is to promote industry, revitalize industry, and strive to increase domestic production, in order to seek the prosperity of the social economy. What I hate is that our people have a common problem, that is, they have no persistence, and are regarded by foreigners as a five-minute fever. If our China has been able to resist inferior goods and promote domestic products in a consistent way in recent years, then now I am afraid that we will not suffer this kind of trampling. However, the past is not to be blamed, and the future can be pursued. From now on, I hope that merchants all over the country will work together and bury themselves in their work, not afraid of not having significant effects. Can students not kill the enemy to save the country? Who says they can't? Today's students should know that ("Saving the country requires reading, and reading is saving the country.") Mr. Wu Zhihui once said that everyone should advocate national salvation through machinery at this time of national crisis. Our young students should pay special attention to this sentence. You were born in China with unsound guns and weapons and backward science. If you want to save China, you must deliberately pursue science and study mechanics to manufacture new weapons to prepare for national use, and to breathe a long sigh of relief for the hundreds of thousands of martyrs who sacrificed in the enemy's artillery fire and bombs. This is the expectation of the people of the country for young students to save the country through science. Quickly work hard to create. Workers and farmers can also save the country by working hard from their positions. For example, increasing the quantity of production and enriching the social economy are all elements that contribute to the strength of the country. However, now the worker tide is surging and industry is not prosperous, and workers and capital seem to be unable to coexist and cooperate sincerely. The newspapers every day are filled with reports of strikes at Factory A or disturbances at Factory B. This phenomenon is certainly not a blessing for society. I hope that the workers will be patient for a while, avoid the debate of emotions, and jointly seek to revitalize industry, in order to achieve the goal of enriching the country and benefiting the people. As for the farmers, they should also adopt new methods to increase agricultural products. Our country has always been based on agriculture, but now rice, wheat, and other categories must be purchased from abroad, which is no wonder. On the one hand, we certainly hope that those who are dedicated to the farmer movement can think about how to improve farmers' knowledge and improve their lives. On the other hand, we also hope to introduce new methods from Europe and the United States as much as possible and engage in imitation. I heard that in Western countries, airplanes are used to sow seeds in agricultural affairs. Looking back at our country, artificial sowing is still used. Isn't the difference too far? In short, workers and farmers should now strive to increase various production and enrich the economy. This is the most important part of the national mobilization sound. Speaking of the army, it is extremely important in the country where a strong neighbor is invading the land and losing territory today. A country raises troops for a thousand days and uses them for a day. At this time, it is time for soldiers to be loyal to the country and sacrifice their lives. We hope that the soldiers who lead the troops across the country will kill to the northeast and fight the Japanese invaders to the death. One day, the lost land will be recovered and they will return in triumph. This is the supreme glory of the soldiers. The degree of danger of our country today is like a thousand pounds hanging by a thread. Strive to save the country and do not hesitate any longer. National mobilization, now is the time! I hope that compatriots across the country will grit their teeth and work hard, doing as much as they can and taking as many steps as they can. Don't be discouraged, don't be disappointed, be resolute and brave, always keep in mind the anti-Japanese war, and never forget saving the country in everything. Then, in one or two years, it will not be difficult for China to wash away the past humiliation and enter the ranks of the great powers. Everyone works hard!

New Postage Rate for Nanyang 87

To Be Implemented on May 1st

According to the Central News Agency, regarding the post office's proposed revision of the postage rate for batch letters to Nanyang, a senior official of the Postal Administration stated the following:

Postage to Singapore Has Increased According to reports from the Shantou and Xiamen post offices, the postage for batch letters sent from the Nanyang Islands and the Malayan Federation has increased from 6 Singapore cents to 8 Singapore cents per letter. Inquiries were sent to the Kuala Lumpur Postal Administration to verify, and it was implemented on October 1st of last year. It was found that since the Republic of China 19, our country and the Kuala Lumpur Post Office have been charging half the international postage for Nanyang letters. Now, the Kuala Lumpur Post Office has increased it from 6 Singapore cents to 8 Singapore cents per letter, which is two-thirds of its international postage (12 cents). In normal circumstances, our country can also handle it in the same way, charging two-thirds of the international postage (25 cents) for a national currency of 16.5 cents.

Our Country Still Charges Half According to the Postal Administration, in order to understand the difficulties of overseas Chinese, it is still planned to maintain the principle of charging half the rate, only revising it to 12.5 cents according to the gold franc exchange rate, which is a special preference.

Revised Rate Does Not Increase Burden According to the survey, when overseas Chinese in Nanyang remit money, they mostly prepay the return (ie, reply) postage at the local rate. The current 8 Singapore cents is approximately equal to 16 cents in national currency, which is more than one-quarter higher than the proposed revised postage of 12.5 cents in our country. Therefore, the proposed revision of the postage rate does not actually increase the burden on overseas Chinese themselves or their families, and is very different from ordinary price increases.

Scheduled Implementation of New Rate The post office originally planned to implement the revised rate as soon as possible, but in order to make all parties understand the truth, it had to explain in detail, which led to delays. Now the post office's economy is becoming increasingly short, and since the loss of the Rehe province, it has become even more difficult. This revision plan must be implemented. It is reported that a notice will be issued to collect batch letter postage according to the new rate from May of this year. When the batch letter rate was revised in 19 years, it started on May 1st, so this time it is also planned to be implemented from May 1st, which is seven months later than the two-time fee increase date of Singapore Post. It can be seen that our country's post office is very preferential to batch letters.

Wusong Vehicle Tax Reduced by Two Months 93

Wusong city is most lively in spring and autumn. In spring, there is the yellow croaker on the market, and merchants from the interior use rickshaws to transport the yellow croaker to Luodian Baoshan Yuepu Yangxing and other places for sale. In autumn, various villages transport the harvested cotton to Wusong for the market. Therefore, in these two seasons, villagers gather in Wusong, and the Wusong market feels lively. Since the establishment of the levy office in the port by the city's Finance Bureau, this type of rickshaw has been levied according to regulations. However, in order to avoid the levy, merchants and villagers in the interior have changed their routes to other ports. Wusong's commerce has declined since the war last year, and the population has decreased. Recently, due to the disappearance of villagers, the situation has become more desperate. Therefore, the Wusong branch office of the City Chamber of Commerce submitted a report to the City Chamber of Commerce, which was forwarded to the Municipal Government, which instructed the Municipal Finance Bureau that the tax should be exempted. The municipal government then instructed the finance and public works bureaus to deliberate, and according to the reply, the matters stated by the association were not entirely false. The municipal government then instructed the Municipal Finance Bureau that all vehicle taxes would be temporarily reduced for two months from April of this year, and previous outstanding taxes would be paid according to regulations. All small vehicles that have not been licensed must still be reported to the Wusong Vehicle Office of the Public Works Bureau for registration, and the lead donation certificate must be obtained from the Wusong Vehicle Donation Office of the Finance Bureau every month. Each vehicle is only charged a certificate fee of five points, to show sympathy.

Tragic Accidents at Two Rubber Factories 95

The City General Labor Union Issues a Declaration

The Shanghai City General Labor Union, yesterday, regarding the tragic accidents that occurred at the Zhen Tai and Yong He rubber factories, issued a declaration saying, "It has been found that in the past month, the Zhen Tai and Yong He rubber factories experienced unprecedented tragedies due to boiler explosions, resulting in hundreds of male and female workers being injured or killed. The dead had broken hands and feet, scorched heads and faces, a truly unbearable sight. The wails and cries of the grieving families embracing the remains were heartbreaking to hear. According to the investigation conducted by this Union regarding the true cause of the accidents, it was entirely due to the factory's desire to increase productivity, which led them to recklessly operate the boilers beyond their original capacity, resulting in this unfortunate tragedy. In addition, the factory's equipment was rudimentary, which made it impossible for the workers to escape the dangerous situation when the accidents occurred, ultimately leading to their deaths in the inferno. Tracing the origin of the disaster, the factory should bear the responsibility for indirect homicide. However, recent advertisements published by the factories claimed that the post-accident arrangements had been completely resolved. The true situation remains vague, and no definite announcement has been made. For the sake of the lives of the workers, for the safety of the workers in the future, and for the sake of humanity, this Union cannot remain silent. A worker toils with their blood and sweat, working hard to earn a meager wage to support their family. If they suddenly suffer an accident, or become disabled, how will their family survive in the future? Therefore, from a humanitarian standpoint, the factories should find ways to provide generous compensation so that the surviving family members can live out their lives. However, they are now casually settling the matter with a mere few hundred yuan, which not only disregards the livelihoods of the bereaved families but also disrespects the lives of the workers. Therefore, at a minimum, they should act in accordance with the provisions of the Factory Law. Secondly, since the cause of this disaster was due to the factory's rudimentary equipment and mismanagement, the factory cannot escape the responsibility for indirect homicide, even if they offer excuses. Furthermore, the personnel responsible for supervising the boilers are the criminals in this case and should not be allowed to go unpunished. Therefore, in addition to providing generous compensation to the families of the deceased, the instigators should be severely punished, brought to justice, to deter future incidents, and to redress the injustice. Thirdly, since these factories caused a tragedy due to negligence, we hope that these factories and other factories will urgently improve their equipment in the future. They must pay close attention to the safety and life protection of the workers, so as to avoid the recurrence of tragic accidents and to value human life. The above three points are the responsibilities of this Union, and we pledge to do our best to fight to the end. We hope that people from all walks of life will stand on the grounds of humanitarianism and impose fair sanctions." This is our declaration.

The Xi Longsheng Case

The Issue of Mother-Son Identity 96

Longsheng's Mother is Lonely and Helpless

Continues to Seek Alimony

Xi Longsheng, a prominent paint merchant residing at No. 4 Songshan Road in the French Concession, also known as Xi Shishang, is currently involved in a lawsuit in the First Special District Court with Ms. Huang Zhou, who resides at No. 50 Kangti Road, regarding the issue of their mother-son relationship. Previously, the late paint merchant tycoon Xi Eming and his younger brother Exian jointly established the Rui Kang Paint Company on Shandong Road, which flourished, accumulating assets of hundreds of thousands of dollars each. Later, Eming married Ms. Huang, but they had no children for a long time. Ms. Huang, considering herself young, did not allow Eming to take concubines. However, Eming's mother was very eager to have a grandson, so she asked her cook, Li Ruilin from Nanjing, to find a boy for Eming to adopt. At that time, during the Guangxu period, Li Ruilin often went to the Nanjing Road Tie Fangzi vegetable market to buy vegetables, where he met a Suzhou woman named Huang Zhou, who sold bean sprouts. Huang Zhou was pregnant at the time, heavily pregnant, so he told her that his master, Xi's old lady, wanted to adopt a boy for Eming. If she gave birth to a boy, would she be willing to let the Xi family adopt him? Huang Zhou, considering herself still young, already had two sons and a large family to feed, making a living difficult. Moreover, since the Xi family was wealthy, she readily agreed, making an agreement while she was still pregnant. The following year, on January 30th of the thirty-first year of Guangxu, Huang Zhou went into labor and gave birth to a boy at noon. After notifying the Xi family, Eming's female servant, Aqiao, and two other relatives went to Huang Zhou's house that night to take the baby. First, they placed him in a matchmaking shop on Baike Road, where Li Ruilin hired a wet nurse to feed him for three or four months. Later, Eming became seriously ill, so they took the child to ward off bad luck. Eming's illness indeed improved, and Eming was overjoyed, naming him Longsheng. His wife, Ms. Huang, mistakenly believing rumors that her husband had an affair, suspected that Longsheng was born to a mistress, and became very jealous. She once attempted suicide by swallowing gold, but was discovered by her family and rescued. After her aunt explained the adoption in detail, they lived in peace. When Eming passed away, due to the family rule that different surnames cannot disrupt the ancestral lineage, his brother Exian's son was established as the heir. Last year, Longsheng was already twenty-seven years old and married Bei Runsheng's daughter as his wife, and had two sons. After Longsheng was taken away by the Xi family, Huang Zhou's husband, Jinlong, and her two sons died one after another. Lonely and destitute, her life became increasingly difficult. Thinking that she still had one child, who had been taken away, she searched everywhere for Li Ruilin. After half a year, she finally met him on Nanjing Road. Li Ruilin told her that the son who was taken away was Xi Longsheng, who now lives at No. 4 Songshan Road. Huang Zhou was overjoyed, believing that she would have food and clothing from now on and a reliable source of support for the rest of her life. She happily went to the address, but Xi's residence was heavily guarded, and she was stopped by the guards and patrolmen, unable to enter. The iron gate was close at hand, but as distant as clouds in the sky. Huang Zhou had to return disappointed. Later, she went again, but was again turned away and ignored. Helpless, she entrusted Wu Jingxiong, a lawyer, to send a letter requesting alimony, but Longsheng still ignored her. Therefore, in December of the previous year, she reported to the French Concession Police Department and filed a public lawsuit against him in the Second Special District Court for abandonment. Xi Longsheng evaded appearing in court, and his uncle Huang Baohua came forward to mediate, ordering Huang Zhou to first withdraw the lawsuit to facilitate the process. Later, Xi Longsheng gave 15,000 yuan to lawyer Wu to transfer to Huang Zhou, who issued a receipt and took it away. For some unknown reason, Huang Zhou actually received 500 yuan, which was not enough to pay off her debts, so she first entrusted lawyer Ma Hongyuan to send a letter requesting continued alimony, but it was left unanswered for a long time. Then she entrusted lawyers Zhang Shewo and Ma Hongyuan to publish a warning in the newspaper. Xi Longsheng then hired lawyers Li and Qin, and filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against Huang Zhou for extortion and defamation. The court approved the request, and the eighth courtroom was opened for trial at 3:00 PM on the 16th. Xi Longsheng arrived in court with lawyer Li Zuyu, protected by Chinese and Western bodyguards. Huang Zhou also arrived with her defense lawyers Zhang Shizhao, Zhang Shewo, and Ma Hongyuan. Judge Wu Zehan presided over the trial. First, Xi Longsheng stated the reasons for the lawsuit. After being questioned by Judge Wu, Huang Zhou replied that Xi Longsheng was indeed her biological son, who was taken away while still in her womb, and now he refuses to recognize his biological mother and even sues his mother, which is truly a rare occurrence in the world. Then, lawyers Zhang Shizhao, Zhang Shewo, and Ma Hongyuan stood up one after another to state that the previous settlement had flaws and that the defendant would file a lawsuit to confirm the mother-son relationship as a remedy. They requested that the court suspend the trial proceedings in this case. Subsequently, due to the issue of summoning witnesses, the lawyers on both sides had a slight debate. Judge Wu ruled that the witnesses would be summoned to court for questioning next Thursday.

Small Kidnapping Case Solved 97

Young Victim Jiang Atang Reclaimed

Kidnapping Ring Leader Wang Desheng Captured

Jiang Desheng of the Western District Sino-Foreign Telephone Company, who resides at No. 45 Jianye Lane, Fulvli Road, in the French Concession, was targeted by criminals because he had some savings. Jiang had a son named Atang, who was only six years old. On the afternoon of January 13th, at 3:00 PM, he was playing in the alley and suddenly went missing. They immediately searched everywhere but could not find him, so they reported to the police station and requested an investigation. Soon, they received eight letters from the kidnappers, demanding 15,000 yuan, and they learned that he had been kidnapped. They reported to the police station's special branch. Inspector Jin Jiulin, along with detectives Zhang Ziying, deputy detectives Zhou Yaoting, Zhou Bingcheng, and patrol officers, disguised themselves and went to No. 22 Fuxiang Spinning Society on Guangxi Road, where they arrested two men from Shaoxing, Zhou Liansheng and Zhang Hualang. They also arrested an accomplice, Fei Zhaojun, inside No. 438 on the same road. They confessed that the victim was hidden in the pavilion of No. 30 Wufuli Lane, Tokyo Road, in Huxi. So, at around 1:00 AM yesterday morning, they cooperated with Chinese and Western detectives from the Putuo Road police station to crack the case. They rescued the victim and arrested a female guard on the spot, taking them all to the police station for transfer to the court for trial. The family of the victim was notified to retrieve him. The police learned that the mastermind of the kidnapping was Wang Desheng (from Shaoxing), who was hiding at No. 249 Meifang Lane, Robert Sheng Road, in Huxi. Jin Jiulin, Zhou Yaoting, and others, along with the Sixth District Branch of Robert Sheng Road, secretly surrounded the address at 1:00 PM yesterday. The detectives bravely rushed in and captured the ringleader Wang Desheng, bringing him back to the police station to await transfer to the court for trial. From this point on, a kidnapping case was completely solved.

In order to promote factory inspections in the Special District, the Chinese Factory Inspection Association has been consulting with relevant groups for days. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, a tea party was held at the YMCA on the ninth floor of the Baxianqiao to invite public groups. Representatives such as Zhong Shaoqin from the Shanghai YWCA, Yu Dehuan from the Shanghai YMCA Shanghai Hai Commune, Cao Yunxiang from the Industrial and Commercial Management Association and labor advisor to the British-American Tobacco Company, and Cheng Haifeng from the China Branch of the International Labour Office, and Tao Leqin from the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession, a dozen or so representatives, were received by Tian Heqing and Li Shude from the association. They discussed inspection matters and exchanged opinions. It is reported that the results were very satisfactory, and they will probably conduct several more consultations before proceeding. However, the date of the official inspection of factories in the Special District will be announced after the municipal government issues an order.

Ancient Tomb Discovered North of the Airport 112

The Corpse's Face as White as Life

North of the Hongqiao Road Airport in Huxi, at the northeast corner of the Xie Family Lane, there is a gray burial tomb covered in weeds, unattended. Recently, the landlord Song Shunsheng (resident of No. 19 Xie Family Lane) excavated the tomb, and there were two coffins containing ashes and corpses. The one on the west (female) had completely decayed, with only a few strands of hair remaining. The coffin on the east was intact and undamaged. Song used an axe to split open the coffin lid, revealing a white-bearded male corpse more than a foot long, with a face as white as life, not decayed. The burial clothes he was wearing were of Ming Dynasty style and were also stripped off by Song Shunsheng and abandoned in the river. Bi Zhenhua, the head of the Sixth District One Branch in charge of the area, learned of this, and, considering that the landlord Song Shunsheng had excavated an ancient tomb and abandoned the corpse in the river, which violated human ethics, immediately ordered the police to arrest Song and investigate the matter. At the same time, he personally conducted an on-site investigation to determine the surname and descendants of the deceased, in order to rebury the remains and preserve the ancient tomb.

Three Koreans Arrested Last Night 121

The Japanese consulate police, having learned that Koreans residing in Shanghai were plotting to assassinate a certain important Japanese person, had previously arrested many people. Last night at around 9 p.m., at the Songjiangchun Restaurant on Wuchang Road in Hongkou, Japanese police, together with detectives, arrested three Koreans and confiscated two pistols and two bombs. They were taken to the Japanese consulate for interrogation.

Medical Community 122

Ling Tongbo Comes to Shanghai for Consultation - Renowned national doctor Ling Tongbo, a specialist in mental illnesses, is well-known far and wide. Those suffering from serious mental illnesses who seek his treatment invariably recover. Starting today, every third and eighth day of the month, he will be available for consultations at the Tianfu Gongji Inn in Guixingdongli, Baoshan Street, Wuma Road.

Ren Nongxuan Pediatric Clinic Relocates - Renowned specialist in pediatric massage, pustules, and general pediatrics, Dr. Ren Nongxuan, has been serving in Shanghai for over twenty years. He has served as director of major hospitals in the area for many years, curing countless difficult and severe pediatric cases. It is recently learned that Dr. Ren's original clinic was insufficient for his needs, so he has relocated to a three-story Western-style building opposite the China Hotel at the western end of Ningbo Road, Zhejiang Road, where he will continue to provide consultations.

Miscellaneous News 123

New News from the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center - In addition to guidance on further education and employment, the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center has recently paid close attention to guidance on health laws. The center has compiled a book, "Health Law Guidance," which contains articles on various health and legal issues written by health mentors Wang Yugang, Zeng Liqun, Zhang Zhongming, Ge Chenghui, Song Guobin, Huang Rixiang, Xu Jihua, Yang Bao, Wang Zhenchuan, Chen Bangdian, and legal mentors Shen Qi, Yuan Yang'an, Huang Zixiong, Yu Yuan, Zhu Shaowen, Wang Zhengshao, Li Zhongdao, Qian Jianqiu, Peng Wangyin, and Shan Yuhua. Everyone should have a copy of this book, which costs one dime for printing costs. Reservations can be made at the center, and it will be published soon. In addition, health mentor Wang Yugang recently wrote a book, "Self-Treatment for Sexual Neurasthenia," which discusses youth sexuality issues in detail and is highly valuable. Furthermore, the center, in light of the courageous resistance of the Northeastern Volunteer Army, sent letters of introduction to those who have achieved success, urging them and their relatives and friends to do their best to solicit donations. They have already collected 300 yuan and have wired the money to General Zhu Ziqiao for emergency needs at the front. The names of all donors will be disclosed in the center's February social affairs monthly report.

Lively Baby Contest - The Lively Baby Contest of the Shanghai English Times newspaper has reportedly received hundreds of photos of Chinese babies from Shanghai and other places since it began. As the contest date approaches, the deadline for submissions is nearing. It is also reported that the newspaper has invited Mrs. Xia Peng, Mrs. Guo Huide, Mrs. Hu Yukeng, Mr. Li Yuanxin, and Dr. Luo Sifu as judges for the Chinese entries.

Special Class Established by Women's Harmonica Society - Since the beginning of the semester, the Shanghai Women's Harmonica Society, located in Xieqiao, has seen a surge in membership. Classes were originally scheduled for Mondays and Fridays at 4 p.m. It has been reported that due to the inconvenience for those learning from far away, a special class has been established at the request of more than 20 female comrades. Class time will be on Sundays from 2 p.m. to 4 p.m. The fee is only five jiao per month, and the course can be completed in two months. The class is scheduled to begin this Sunday (the 19th). Those who are interested in studying the harmonica, whether they have studied before or not, can register at the Shanghai Girls' Middle School, No. 81 Manufacturing Bureau Road, Xieqiao, Nanshi. Course details will be sent upon request.
